Academia Sinica Organizes a Marine Product Survey Team 169

Dividing into Four Areas, Phased Exploration, and Borrowing Warships to Assist the Work

The Institute of Zoology and Botany of Academia Sinica recently organized a marine product survey team to study China's marine products and assist in the development of fisheries production. It is stipulated that it will take four years to complete all the work. The details are recorded as follows:

Regional Measurement 170

In order to study the depth and salinity of seawater in the coastal provinces of China, as well as the growth conditions of animals and plants such as fish, shellfish, seaweed, and algae, Academia Sinica has specially organized a survey team to conduct on-site research, record it faithfully, and contribute to the domestic academic community and fishery-related organizations to increase marine product harvests. Regarding the scope of the survey, it has now been stipulated that the coastal areas of China will be divided into four regions: the first region is the Bohai Sea, from Weihaiwei to Qinhuangdao; the second region is the Yellow Sea, from Zhejiang to Jiangsu; the third region is the East China Sea, from Zhejiang to Fujian; and the fourth region is the South China Sea, from Fujian to Guangdong. In addition to accurate measurement and chemical testing, biological surveys will be conducted at any time. It is planned to survey the first region in the first year, the second region in the second year, the third region in the third year, and the fourth region in the fourth year.

Borrowing Warships 171

The institute is conducting the above work with the survey team.

The above work will take a long time, and it will be difficult to achieve results without larger ships and comprehensive equipment. Last year, staff were sent to Weihaiwei to inspect and to Qingdao to meet with Xie Gangzhe, commander of the Fourth Fleet, to discuss the matter of borrowing warships. Xie agreed to provide full assistance. At the beginning of this month, Cai Yuanpei, president of Academia Sinica, sent a letter to Xie requesting permission to borrow warships. Recently, Xie replied, stating that the Ninghai warship could be allocated for use. The ship has a deadweight of 1,200 tons and is fully equipped, which can provide maximum service for the survey team. It is now reported that the survey team will be organized by the institute at the end of March after personnel are assigned, and will depart at the beginning of April to start the first year of work in the first region.

British Consulate Continues to Try the Case of a British Woman Manufacturing Narcotics 172

Monthly Income of 400 Yuan, Expenses of More Than 1,000 Yuan

Where Does the Shortfall Come From? Considered Suspicious

According to the "Da Mei Evening News," the case of the wife of Johnson, a British resident at 361 Avenue Foch, being accused of illegally manufacturing narcotics in her residence was heard again by the police court of the British Consulate this morning (the 23rd). First, the defendant's lawyer, Blanc, cross-examined Walker, a chemist from the Public Health Department of the Municipal Council, to prove that the defendant could not hear the sound or smell the odor when the machine for manufacturing narcotics was in operation. Then, Western Detective Dunn testified that when he entered the main room that day, he saw thick carpets on the floor, and a carpet was also laid on the ladder. A box containing batteries was placed under a Chinese mattress that was about half an inch thick. After the testimony, Blanc stated that his client was completely unaware of the manufacturing of narcotics in her home until the detectives discovered the machine for manufacturing narcotics in the main room of her home. Now, those who had been to her home in December can be invited to testify that they had never seen anything suspicious or smelled anything unusual. Blanc then cross-examined the defendant. The defendant looked nervous and testified that she was 36 years old and came to China in early 1914. She taught in Tianjin for seven and a half years, and then came to Shanghai to teach for several years. Later, she went to Yantai and Weihaiwei to work as a teacher for several months. In 1925, she returned to Shanghai and taught English at two Chinese schools. In 1931, she married Johnson. Her husband was an Australian who had served in the Australian Navy. After marriage, they lived together on Rue Seymore. In the summer of 1932, her husband worked for a shipping company. In September of the same year, they went to England together, coming to China on the Shandong steamship. Her husband then lost his job for more than a year. Later, he helped the Dalu Industrial Company prepare to purchase a ship, but he was not paid. Last December, the company hired him to go to England to sail the purchased ship to China, with a monthly salary of 400 yuan. He departed from Shanghai on December 11. Her husband wanted to do business in Shanghai during his unemployment, but he failed. His father helped him with 150 pounds sterling. Last year, a certain charity organization did lend him money to help him with his urgent needs. Before departing for England, the Dalu Industrial Company paid him 1,000 yuan. Her husband had no bank savings. When she left Shanghai, she promised to remit money at any time to cover household expenses. Her husband bought a car in early December of last year, paying 255 yuan per month. The lease for the residence on Avenue Foch was for one year, with a monthly rent of 390 yuan. The rent was indeed high, but she loved it because it had a large garden and clean air. She planned to sublet it to others in the summer. Her husband had hired a cook, a shop assistant, a driver, and a "Xiao Xixue," each with a monthly salary of 100 yuan, all recommended by a certain Chinese engineer known to her husband. According to the defendant's testimony, Johnson's household expenses, excluding food and clothing, were 1,045 yuan per month, while her monthly income was only 400 yuan. The defendant could not explain where the monthly shortfall came from. It is reported that Johnson departed from England for Shanghai on January 21. According to a telegram he sent to his lawyer, his wife was unaware of the situation. After he arrives in Shanghai, he plans to investigate the servants he hired, and the truth will come to light.

Car Driver Causes Accident, Injuring Pedestrians 173

Sent to Two Hospitals in Nanshi for Treatment

A Worker Dies from His Injuries

| The Driver Who Caused the Accident Was Handed Over to the Bureau for Legal Action |

The public bus operated by the Municipal Public Utility Bureau had a breakdown at Xiaonanmen Station at around 3 PM yesterday, so the bureau sent Lu A'er (age 29), a native of Haimen driving vehicle No. 82, to the scene to repair it. While driving north to south on Minguo Road outside Xiaobeimen in Nanshi, he carelessly crashed into Wang Deqing (age 28), a native of Nanjing residing at No. 15 Fenqingfang, next to Xiafeifang on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, who was riding bicycle No. 4078. The bicycle was not only damaged, but Wang's right leg was also crushed, bleeding profusely, and he was seriously injured. Lu, panicking, crashed into Shen Renhua (age 32), a native of Yancheng, pulling a rickshaw and Li Weichuan (age 50), a native of Ningbo, as well as Xu Tiande (age 36), a native of Yancheng, pulling a rickshaw with a female passenger near the Huashang tram station on Fangbang Bridge. The male passenger's waist and the female passenger's head were injured on both sides. They immediately hired rickshaws and went to the hospital for treatment. In addition to the rickshaw puller Shen Renhua injuring his left hand and buttocks, and Xu Tiande injuring his left foot and internally, Kong Luoshi, a 78-year-old woman from Zhenjiang, was injured on her right hand and both sides of her head, as well as Shen A'bin, a native of Lishui pushing a cart on Broadway in Hongkou, on his face, and another worker whose name is unknown. The driver, Lu A'er, was taken into custody by police officer Zhang Xuezeng from Post No. 17. Police officer Zhang Xuezeng from Post No. 16 used the telephone to notify the Western District Fire Brigade to dispatch an ambulance to send the seriously injured worker, whose name is unknown, to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, and sent Huang Fuqing, the old woman Kong Laosi, and cart pusher Shen A'bin to Qu Zhibu Hospital on Penglai Road for treatment. The rickshaw pullers Shen Renhua and Xu Tiande were slightly injured and were sent to Qu Zhibu Hospital for treatment after the police officer registered their cases. It is reported that the driver, Lu A'er, has been handed over to the General Bureau for legal action. However, the worker, whose name is unknown, died shortly after being sent to Shanghai Hospital due to serious injuries.

Suicide by Gunshot Due to Unbearable Illness 174

Long Kehou's Body Was Examined Yesterday

Long Kehou, 32, a native of Huai'an and former director of the Anhui Provincial Military Law Department, resided at No. 16 Jingyuli, Weihaiwei Road. Recently, he suffered from severe lung disease. Although he had consulted famous Chinese and Western doctors, it was ineffective. An X-ray examination revealed that his lungs were irreparably ulcerated. On the day before, Long felt unbearable pain due to this disease and developed suicidal thoughts. At around 4 PM, while his family members were not in the room, he took his own pistol and fired a shot at his throat. After Xu Ziyu, the attendant, heard the sound and went to check, he found Long lying in a pool of blood. He immediately notified his wife, Qin, who sent him to Baolong Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died shortly thereafter. The hospital reported it to the Chengdu Road Police Station, which sent detectives to investigate. The body was then taken to the Forensic Examination Office on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Court, arrived at the office to examine the body. After questioning, Long Qin, the deceased's wife, testified to the above. Guo then ruled that the deceased, Long Kehou, was male and died from a gunshot wound during his lifetime. The body was handed over to his wife, Long Qin, who signed a guarantee to claim it for coffin and burial.

Exquisite Opium Pipe 175

The Stem and Bowl Are Fully Inlaid with Silver

Also Has a Silver-Engraved Seven-Character Poem

And Embedded Diamonds, Emeralds, Etc.

Chen Wanpeng Fined 500 Yuan for Smoking Opium

Chen Wanpeng (aka Jingzhang), a runner for Yongfeng Qianzhuang from Shaoxing, had an opium addiction. He kept a full set of opium paraphernalia in his residence at No. 9, Lane 170, Carter Road. He would often recline on a couch, indulging in opium smoke. This was discovered by Inspector Gai Wen of the Fourth Detective Squad of the Xinzha Police Station and Detective Xing Peisong, who reported it to the First Special Court and obtained a search warrant. They went to arrest Chen and confiscated six opium pipes, six opium lamps, twelve opium bowls, twenty-four taels of raw opium, three jars of opium paste, weighing five pounds and six ounces, two containers of opium ash, three trays, one pair of pliers, five needles, three pipe racks, etc. The confiscated opium paraphernalia was extremely luxurious. One opium pipe in particular was an unparalleled masterpiece. The stem and bowl were fully inlaid with silver, engraved with delicate flowers, and had a silver-engraved seven-character poem, inlaid with diamonds, emeralds, and other precious stones. It was of considerable value. All of it was taken to the police station. The police chief allowed Chen to be released on bail of 255 yuan. Yesterday morning, Wu Tingqi, a judge from the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special Court, held a trial. The defendant, Chen Wanpeng, hired two lawyers to present the case, stating that some of the confiscated opium paraphernalia belonged to Feng, a tenant downstairs. The defendant previously had a stomach illness, so he sometimes smoked opium, but he did not open the lamp for others to smoke, etc. After reviewing the evidence, Judge Wu Tingqi sentenced Chen Wanpeng to a fine of 500 yuan for possessing opium and opium paraphernalia. If he could not pay the fine, he would be imprisoned at a rate of three yuan per day. The raw opium, opium paste, and opium paraphernalia were confiscated.

Zhang Guanghua's Case of Cutting and Killing His Younger Brother 176

Continued Hearing Tomorrow Afternoon

Zhang Guanghua, a 27-year-old native of Henan, and his 18-year-old younger brother, Zhang Guangzhou, had been living together in a three-story pavilion room at No. 24 Chongdefang, Minguo Road outside Xiaobeimen in the French Concession, for more than a year. At 4:00 AM on November 23 of last year, Zhang Guangzhou was suddenly killed by a sharp blade cutting off his head and neck. Zhang Guanghua also suffered five or six knife wounds to his head and ran out screaming for help. The second landlord notified the police, who took Guanghua to the police station and sent him to the hospital for treatment. After he recovered and was interrogated, the reason for the killing was revealed. Guangzhou attacked his brother with a knife, but Guanghua fought back in self-defense and killed his brother. Guanghua was transferred to the Second Special Court, and the public prosecutor filed a lawsuit against Zhang Guanghua for murder. Judge Xiong Huiping held a court hearing and interrogated him. Zhang Guanghua flatly denied killing his brother, saying that he felt someone killing his brother in his sleep, first cutting his head and then running out screaming for help because there were no electric lights, so he could not clearly see the murderer's face. He was instructed to reschedule the hearing. In the rescheduled hearing, the presiding judge went to the scene of the incident to investigate the situation. It has been reported in the previous two newspapers. Yesterday, another continued hearing was held. Judge Xiong and Clerk Tao Zongkan specially opened the Second Criminal Court for the hearing. Lawyer Yuan Jiahuan appeared in court on behalf of the Police Department, and the official asked the defendant questions. Zhang still denied killing his brother. The statements he made were the same as those recorded in the previous report and will not be repeated. The court believed that the investigation of both facts and evidence had been completed. Because the defense lawyer representing the defendant went to the Suzhou High Court yesterday to appear in court, he requested a reschedule in advance, so he could not begin the argument. The official instructed to reschedule the hearing to 1:30 PM on the 25th (tomorrow). The defendant was still sent back to the detention center.

Daxing's New Steamer, Xinhongxing, Made Its Maiden Voyage to Ningbo Yesterday 177

Satisfactory Test Drive, Hosting Shipping Merchants

Passing Zhenhai Without Stopping for Now

The iron-hulled express steamer "Xinhongxing," ordered by Daxing Shipping Company from Hongchang Machinery Factory in this port, has been fully completed. It replaced the old "Hongxing" steamer on a maiden voyage to Ningbo at 5 PM yesterday. The details are recorded below:

General Information of the New Steamer 178

Daxing Shipping Company believed that the original "Hongxing" steamer sailing on the Shanghai-Ningbo route was smaller and the cabin space was insufficient. It specially ordered a new steamer from Gaochang Temple Hongchang Machinery Shipyard in the winter of the year before last, named "Xinhongxing" to replace the old "Hongxing" steamer for trips to Ningbo. The new steamer has now been fully completed. The hull is 200 feet long, 32 feet wide, and has a draft of 12 feet. The total tonnage of each cabin is 1,259 tons, the net tonnage of the cargo hold is 740 tons, and the hourly speed is about 13 nautical miles. The cost is more than 290,000 yuan in national currency.

Crew Assignment 179

The entire ship has three decks, with four super-class cabins, forty ordinary cabins, more than one hundred lower-class cabins, more than one hundred high berth spaces, more than six hundred steerage berth spaces, and about one hundred lower hold berth spaces. The crew is entirely composed of Chinese, all of whom have been assigned. The shipowner is Fu Anxing, the chief mate is Gu Jude, the second mate is Xu Shansheng, and Chen Hanping is the ship's comprador. The total number of crew members, including sailors and tea boys, is about 300.

Maiden Voyage to Ningbo 180

The ship specially held a test drive on the Huangpu River near Longhua at 2 PM the day before yesterday. The test drive was completed at more than 3 PM. The results of the test drive were satisfactory. At 1 PM yesterday, leaders from the shipping and customs industries were invited to visit the ship at the Daxing Wharf on South Bund. Xu Zhongxin, the manager of the company, personally led the reception. It left port at 5 PM to replace the Hongxing steamer on a maiden voyage to Ningbo.

Zhenhai Does Not Stop 181

According to Xu Zhongxin, the manager of the company, the Xinhongxing steamer will start its maiden voyage today and will depart from Shanghai to Ningbo every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday, and from Ningbo to Shanghai every Tuesday, Thursday, and Saturday. It will pass through Zhenhai, but will not stop for now. Once the company's financial resources are sufficient, it will consider purchasing land in Zhenhai to install a wharf. For now, it is still difficult to talk about.

Rice Prices Are Falling, Need to See Further Reduction 182

Due to Many Orders for Foreign Rice, Wholesalers Are Discouraged

According to Xin Sheng News, rice prices in this city have fallen in recent days due to the cold weather and river freezing, as well as the receding tide, which has cut off the river route in the Jiwangmiao area of ​​West Shanghai, resulting in a shortage of goods. Yesterday, Jiang Shizhi of the Shanghai North Rice Transport Merchants Association went to the Fifth Patrol Team of the Beixinjing Water Patrol. The team sent personnel to the Yujidun Police Station to supervise the patrolmen and try to clear the passage. As a result, the number of ships arriving in Zhabei suddenly increased yesterday, reaching sixty or seventy. However, sales were flat, resulting in a drop of one jiao in each cargo. Changbang Head Rice was 13.4 yuan, Wuxi No. 2 was 12.5 to 11.7 yuan, Su Geng was 11 to 10.8 yuan, and Foreign Rice was 12.3 to 11.5 yuan. According to rice industry observations, the reason for this surge in goods is that the Social Bureau announced many orders for foreign rice, causing wholesalers to lose confidence and sell off their goods. If there are more goods arriving today and tomorrow, it is expected that the rice price will decrease by one jiao before the end of the year.

The Case of Twelve Deaths from Poisoning at a Small Restaurant is Concluded 185

Restaurant Employee Li Caiyin Sheds Tears and Kowtows Unceasingly

The Final Argument Was Concluded Yesterday and the Verdict is Scheduled for the 29th of This Month

The Xieshunxing small restaurant, opened by Han Huatang of Haimen, located at 59 Ouzhou Road, Hongkou, on the noon of November 28th of last year, during the peak time for lunch, diners had just finished eating when an unprecedented tragedy occurred, resulting in the deaths of twelve people, including Liu Koulang. Wu Deyi, the prosecutor of the local court, arrived at the scene to examine and provide coffins for the deceased. The Linping Road Police Station arrested and sent the restaurant employee Li Caiyin to the court for interrogation and detention. The remaining food from the restaurant, such as fish, meat, and vegetables, was sent to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for examination. As previously reported, it is now learned that the case has been thoroughly investigated by Prosecutor Wu, and a murder charge has been filed with the criminal court. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Zhang Shao specially opened the fifth court to hear the case, ordering the detained Li Caiyin to be brought to court for questioning. Li is 43 years old, from Haimen, and works at the Xieshunxing small restaurant. (Question) Who opened the Xieshunxing restaurant? (Answer) Han Huatang opened it. (Question) Who bought the fish? (Answer) The boss bought it. (Question) How much fish did he buy? (Answer) About forty or fifty catties. (Question) What was the shape and color of the fish like? (Answer) Big head, small tail, fat belly, the color was black, I don't know what kind of fish it was. (Question) Do you usually buy this fish? (Answer) No, we don't buy it. (Question) Who washes and cooks the fish? (Answer) The apprentice washes the fish, and the boss cooks it. (Question) What day was the fish bought? (Answer) I forgot the date. (Question) How many employees are there in the restaurant? (Answer) Six people. (Question) Who threw away the remaining two fish? (Answer) The apprentice threw them away. (Question) Where did Han Huatang escape to? (Answer) I don't know. At this point, Prosecutor Wu was invited to the court to make his argument. (Question) Do you have anything else to say? Li listened and shed tears, kowtowing unceasingly, repeatedly proclaiming his innocence. The judge concluded the hearing and scheduled the verdict for 10:00 AM on the 29th of this month. Li Caiyin was returned to custody to await further instructions.

Domestically Produced Satin Hats are Charged According to the Fourth Class 186

The Ministry of Railways Instructs the Railway Bureau to Comply

The Joint Railway Administration recently received Instruction No. 137 from the Ministry of Railways, which stated that the Nanjing Fan and Hat Industry Association submitted a report stating that the goods produced by the members of the association are handmade products with very low prices. The highest wholesale price of satin hats is around 40 cents, and the lowest is only 20 cents. However, the railway classifies satin hats as second class and woolen cloth hats as fourth class. Due to the high freight costs, sales have been sluggish. The association requested a reduction in freight rates. According to the regulations of the cargo classification table, domestically produced satin hats should be charged freight according to the fourth class for ordinary goods. If the association's report that satin hats are charged as second class is true, then the carrier is in error. It is hereby ordered that all railways should charge domestically produced satin hats according to the fourth class. In addition to separate orders and approvals, you are hereby notified. The bureau has already forwarded the order to the Traffic Department for information.

Amendments to the Regulations for Obtaining Licenses for Traditional Chinese Medicine Practitioners 189

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau issued a notice yesterday stating that Article 18 of the "Provisional Regulations for the Management of Physicians (Traditional Chinese Medicine Practitioners) in This City" stipulates that "Each medical clinic's business license should be submitted for annual inspection and re-issuance. Those who fail to submit it for inspection within the deadline will be fined up to five yuan." Recently, the bureau has repeatedly received reports from registered physicians stating that they were unable to comply with the regulations and submit their licenses for inspection within the deadline, either due to the impact of previous wars or due to a lack of understanding of the license inspection deadline. They requested permission to waive the fine and re-inspect the licenses in order to resume their practices. In order to rectify and provide relief, the bureau has submitted a proposal to the municipal government for approval to amend Article 18 of the original regulations to "Each medical clinic's business license should be displayed in a prominent place for public viewing and should be submitted to the Municipal Health Bureau for annual inspection and re-issuance from February 1st to the end of March each year. Those who fail to submit it for inspection within the deadline will be fined up to five yuan each time." With the approval of the municipal government, all medical business licenses that have not been submitted for inspection in the past will be granted a one-time exemption from fines and re-inspection from January 20th to the end of March of this year to show compassion. Those who still fail to comply with the regulations and submit their licenses for inspection after the deadline will be punished according to the regulations. This notice is hereby issued.

The Zhou Exuan Case Concludes with Third Trial 191

Six-Month Sentence Suspended for Three Years

Zhou Exuan, the son of Zhou Weishi, a wealthy Suzhou businessman in Shanghai, indulged in frivolous pleasures and formed an indissoluble bond with the famous prostitute Zhang Zhuying. Exuan then rented a house to hide her. When Weishi learned that Zhang had given birth to a son, he immediately dissolved the small family. Exuan, intimidated by his father's stern reputation, dared not protect her and allowed Zhang to marry someone else. However, Exuan provided monthly funds for the upbringing of their son, Dayuan, who was raised by Zhang. Until the winter of the year before last, when Dayuan was ten years old, the education and upbringing funds suddenly stopped being provided. Zhang, in her capacity as Dayuan's legal guardian, sued Exuan for abandoning his biological son in the First Special District Court. However, the original lawsuit was dismissed in the first instance. Zhang was unwilling to accept this and hired a lawyer to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. After the second instance concluded, Zhou Exuan was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for abandonment. Zhou also claimed to be dissatisfied and appealed to the Supreme Court. The lawsuit has been ongoing for a year now. It is now learned that the third instance of the Supreme Court has also announced its verdict in recent days, rejecting Zhou Exuan's appeal. However, the six-month sentence imposed by the second instance has been suspended for three years.

Catalogue of Scripts from the Hemu Lu Published 195

Divided into Thirty-Four Categories, Totaling More Than Three Thousand Volumes

Book Price Six Yuan, Sold at Shanghai Bank

Mr. Song Chunfang, a former professor at Peking University, is a great enthusiast of opera and drama. He has explored almost ten thousand volumes of secret books from maps and private treasures. Recently, he compiled his collection of Chinese and foreign operas and dramas into a book called "Catalogue of Scripts from the Hemu Lu," totaling more than three thousand types, divided into several categories, such as China, Japan, India, Turkey, Eastern Theatre, Russia, Poland, Spain, Norway, Commentary on Chinese Drama, New Theatre Movement, Playwriting, Modern Drama, Film, Dramatic Criticism, Opera, Acting, History of Drama, etc., with a total of thirty-four categories including appendices. Among them, the rare editions are those that are not seen outside. In his preface, he said, "Since I first went west, I listened to lectures in famous cities and explored books in neighboring countries. What I liked at that time was all in opera and drama. I have explored almost ten thousand volumes of secret books from maps and private treasures. In 1915, I first traveled to Paris and entered the Bibliothegue de l'Opera, where I stayed for three months, forgetting to return. In 1917, I returned to Shanghai, chose what I loved, and brought it back with me. In 1921, I went abroad again and passed through Germany and Austria. At that time, the Great War had just ended and currency values had fallen. I exhausted my savings and bundled them up. Later, due to illness, they were shelved. For the past five or six years, I have been traveling back and forth between Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Tianjin, without a settled place. Last year, I spent four thousand yuan to build Hemu Lu by the seaside in Qingdao, gathering books in it. This spring, I resigned from my position as a Qingdao city councilor and wrote the catalogue on my door, which took a month to complete. In the past twenty years, I have worked hard to search for and acquire no more than three thousand volumes. My wealth and talent are insufficient, and my knowledge is limited. It is not surprising. Fortunately, what I have collected is limited to one category, so it is easier to choose and separate. Even this small collection is rare. In terms of opera and drama, it provides a rough overview. This collection may be the best in China. Compared to the Bibliothegue de l'Opera in Paris, it is only one percent. As for the collection of the Four Treasuries, picking up what has been lost, and filling the shelves with books, it is a public affair and not something that individuals can do. Moreover, accumulation is gradual, and dispersal is impermanent. Not to mention the distant past, recent examples include the Haiyuan Pavilion in Liaocheng and the Ce Hai Tower in Yangzhou, the elites of generations, eventually scattered and lost. What I have now may not be preserved forever, especially with the flames of war looming. After the compilation was completed, I was filled with anxiety, so I recorded my feelings as follows." From this, we can see the difficulty of searching and the precision of storage. This catalogue is bound in one volume and sells for six yuan, sold at the Shanghai Bank Library.

There are four types of passes: Route 1 (North Station to Jiangwan) for 5 yuan per month, Route 3 (North Station to Radio Station) for 6 yuan per month, Routes 1, 4, and 5 (North Station to Jiangwan Municipal Government and Municipal Government Dormitory) for 6 yuan per month, and a general pass for all lines for 10 yuan per month. It is stipulated that sales will begin on the 25th of this month and will take effect from February 1st. Detailed regulations have been established.

Letter from the National Products Factory Association to the Customs Superintendent 202

The Shanghai National Products Factory Association sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office yesterday stating that it had received a letter from the Hangzhou National Products Factory Association, which stated that Wan Zhong Company had sent a letter stating that after participating in the Ningxian National Exhibition, it took the remaining goods on a ship from Ningbo to Shanghai. When it arrived in Shanghai, the goods were detained by customs officers. It was requested to forward a letter for negotiation. The association confirmed that the goods carried by the company were the remaining items from participating in the exhibition. How the customs office should negotiate, it was hoped that the association would handle it nearby. After the association sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs Service, it received a reply stating that the goods seized on the ship were brought in privately by the crew members and would be released upon payment of a fine of one times the value of the goods, together with the transit tax. The Wan Zhong Company went to Ningbo to participate in the exhibition this time under the leadership of the Hangzhou National Products Factory Association. When it opened, the goods from Hangzhou to Ningbo were transported by the Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway and were exempt from taxes according to regulations. This time, the company's representative carried them with him and returned to Hangzhou via Shanghai. The representative was unfamiliar with the customs regulations, which led to this mistake. The situation is still excusable. It is requested that the superintendent examine and approve the transfer to the Jianghai Customs Service to exempt them from punishment and return the detained products in full in order to maintain the national products salvation movement. It is truly in the public interest.

工部局發表人力車夫須知 208

The Public Rickshaw Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council has, since handling the registration of public rickshaw pullers, yesterday issued a set of Rickshaw Puller Guidelines, divided into twenty-nine articles. The full text is transcribed below:

(1) When you are pulling the rickshaw, you must carry your license with you at all times. If you are going out, you can hand the license over to the Municipal Council's Rickshaw Puller Licensing Office for safekeeping to avoid losing it. When you return, you can reclaim it from the original licensing office.

(2) The license armband must be worn on your left arm in a visible place at all times, so that the number can be seen clearly.

(3) You must always obey the traffic directions of the police. The rickshaw owner will tell you about the Municipal Council's traffic regulations, and you must comply.

(4) When your rickshaw is stopped or when passengers are boarding, you must bring the rickshaw close to the side of the road and must not approach the roadside marked with red lines or paved with black and white tiles.

(5) You must pay attention to and obey all police signals.

(6) You must not run in the middle of the road, but should try to walk as close to the left side of the road as possible.

(7) If you have difficulties with the fare, you should report to the nearest policeman or nearby police station for a proper resolution.

(8) When pulling a rickshaw, you must form a single line and cannot have two or three rickshaws running side by side.

(9) You must obey the orders of the police on duty.

(10) If your passenger wants to get out in front of a shop on a busy street, you cannot stop the rickshaw in front of the shop, but should stop in a nearby alley or side street.

(11) If a passenger in your rickshaw becomes ill or dies, report it to the police and ask for their help, or take the passenger to the nearest police station.

(12) Your rickshaw must not carry vegetable market items or other goods that could soil the rickshaw.

(13) When pulling a rickshaw, if you want to turn, you must first make a hand signal to indicate the direction you are turning.

(14) When you want to turn right, you cannot take a shortcut, but must make a wide turn.

(15) Before you stop, you must raise your hand above your head to notify approaching vehicles.

(16) If you encounter an accident, you should stop to help and wait for the police to arrive on the scene to take orders. If there is no policeman nearby, you should immediately report to the nearest police station.

(17) All vehicles that need to stop on Nanjing Road, Jing'an Temple Road, or Route Ghisi, east of Route Ma, must have the left side of the rickshaw close to the roadside.

(18) From sunset to sunrise, you must keep the rickshaw lamp lit.

(19) No vehicle may stop on Nanjing Road for more than thirty minutes between 8:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. daily, except on Sundays and holidays.

(20) You cannot pull an empty rickshaw on Nanjing Road. If your passenger gets out on Nanjing Road, then you must return home from a nearby side street.

(21) You cannot compete for or solicit business, nor can you rush across the road to greet customers.

(22) Items left behind by passengers in the rickshaw must be immediately taken to the nearest police station.

(23) When not in use, the rickshaw door cloth should be placed in the bucket (i.e., the passenger compartment), and you should pay attention to whether the number painted on the door cloth is the same as the plate number.

(24) After you obtain a rickshaw puller's license, you can rent a rickshaw from the rickshaw owner you prefer. At the same time, the rickshaw owner can also rent the rickshaw to the rickshaw puller he prefers. However, we hope that there will be harmonious work between rickshaw owners and rickshaw pullers. When you are about to leave Shanghai, or if you want to change careers and no longer pull a rickshaw, you must notify the rickshaw owner, and he can help you hand over your license and armband to the Municipal Council's Rickshaw Puller Licensing Office for safekeeping.

(25) The Rickshaw Puller Mutual Aid Society was established for your benefit. Your dues of three and a half cents (about eleven copper coins) per shift are used to fund the society. Currently, two society locations have been opened on Dong Jiaxing Road and Route Pottier. In the near future, other locations will continue to be established. The licensing fee of one yuan has already been paid to the Municipal Council by the Mutual Aid Society on your behalf.

(26) The fare schedule on the rickshaw is for passengers to see. If you are willing to charge less, you can do so.

(27) After a shift, the rickshaw should be returned to the rickshaw company and cleaned thoroughly.

(28) The maximum daily rickshaw rental, including the Rickshaw Puller Mutual Aid Society dues, is eighty-five cents. If the rickshaw owner wants to charge you more, you can report it to the Municipal Council's Rickshaw Affairs Committee. If you owe the rickshaw owner a debt, rent, or owe money to the labor union, then you must pay it separately from the rickshaw rental, and you should obtain a separate receipt for the payment. Also, in the event of such incidents, the rickshaw owner must have a written document stating the amount of debt owed by the rickshaw puller, etc. Afterwards, each repayment of debt or other payments by the rickshaw puller must be recorded in detail for inspection by the Municipal Council's Rickshaw Affairs Committee.

(29) You must absolutely comply with the Rickshaw Puller License Regulations. If you violate any article, your license will be revoked, and then you will have no chance to pull a rickshaw again.

Educational News

倫敦中國藝展關於選擇保險各問題 215

London Chinese Art Exhibition Regarding Selection and Insurance Issues

▲ 籌委會函復陶孟和等

The Organizing Committee Responds to Tao Menghe and Others

▲ 擇要說明未嘗涉苟且

A Concise Explanation: No Negligence Involved

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 23rd) Regarding the London Chinese Art Exhibition, academics such as Tao Menghe have expressed opinions on issues such as selection and insurance. The Organizing Committee recently responded to Tao et al. in a letter, stating: "We recently read in the January 20th Ta Kung Pao the concerns of Mr. and others regarding the London Art Exhibition and the importance of caution. Your intentions are commendable, but the actual situation may not be fully understood. Therefore, we provide a concise explanation as follows:

(1) Origin: This matter was originally initiated by British academics, jointly with the British Royal Academy of Arts, who formally proposed to our country that the spirit of Chinese art, which transcends daily material life, has a stimulating effect on the Western people. In recent years, countries such as Italy and France have exhibited art in London, and the relationship between England and these countries has often been significantly enhanced. China, as the ancestor of Eastern culture, if it can hold an international exhibition in London, its effect will be significant. Under this consideration, our government has granted permission, and for the sake of caution, requested that the British government jointly host it. The British have formally declared their cooperation.

(2) Decision-Making Process: Before the government accepted the British proposal for this art exhibition, it first sought the opinion of the Board of Directors of the Old Palace Museum. The museum resolved to approve its principles. Subsequently, Wang Jingwei, Chiang Kai-shek, and other officials also issued documents and telegrams in support of the proposal. It was then successively submitted to the Executive Yuan and the Central Political Council for discussion and decision.

(3) Security Issues: This issue has also been repeatedly submitted to the Board of Directors of the Old Palace Museum for discussion. The board believes in focusing on practical safeguards and not being constrained by insurance. Later, this committee presented the issue to the Executive Yuan for approval, which decided that practical safety measures should be sought. The reason for the Yuan's decision was that insurance would require a large sum of insurance premiums and would not increase the safety of the items. The government attaches importance to the safety of the items themselves. In accordance with this decision, the committee solemnly telegraphed to the British that if there are no effective ways to guarantee safety, this matter may end in suspension. Therefore, in order to prevent piracy and other accidents, the British formally notified that they are willing to send warships to escort the postal ships carrying the exhibits. In order to reduce difficulties and accidents at the time of entry, the British side also intends not to inspect the items at customs when they arrive in England, but to inspect them together with Chinese representatives at the exhibition venue. In addition, the British Foreign Office stated that it is willing to do its best to assist in all other safety matters. Detailed measures have been drafted and will be announced separately.

(4) Right to Select Exhibits: The initial selection of exhibits will be handled by the Chinese side. The British committee members may make suggestions after the initial selection, but their suggestions will not take effect without the consent of the Chinese side. For items that the Chinese side believes cannot be taken abroad, they can certainly not be taken abroad. Therefore, the final selection right for the exhibits actually belongs to the Organizing Committee.

(5) Duration of Exhibits Leaving the Country: The total time required for the exhibits to leave the country this time, including the round trip and the time required for the exhibition in England, should be no more than ten months. The outside world's assumption that it will take a year and a half or two years is not true.

(6) Quantity and Quality of Exhibits Going Abroad: The ancient relics of the Old Palace Museum to be selected this time are limited to a very small portion of the ancient relics stored in Shanghai by the Old Palace Museum. Together with other items solicited, the total will be no more than 1,500 pieces. All national treasures with special historical value that have been recognized by special committees will not be taken abroad. This has been repeatedly resolved by the Board of Directors of the Old Palace Museum and this committee, and has been formally informed to the British committee members.

In summary, the government and this committee have handled this matter without any negligence."

教部嚴令平私立華北學院結束 216

Ministry of Education Strictly Orders the Closure of the Private North China College in Peiping

(Nanjing, 23rd) The person in charge of the Ministry of Education stated that the private North China College in Peiping was approved by the Ministry in August of the 20th year for temporary establishment, and listed several points, setting a one-year deadline for improvement. If it failed to comply within the deadline, the establishment would be revoked. In July of the 21st year, the Ministry sent personnel to inspect the college and found that the points for improvement in the previous order had not been complied with within the deadline, so the establishment was revoked immediately. In January of the previous year, the college was instructed to close down as soon as possible. In May, the Peiping Municipal Social Affairs Bureau was ordered to transfer instructions to stop enrollment. In August, the Social Affairs Bureau was telegraphed again to strictly prohibit enrollment. Last year, the Ministry of Education sent personnel to inspect universities in Peiping and Tianjin, and conveniently went to the college to inspect the closure situation. No one was in charge of the college, the administration was not on track, and it was found that there were still violations of the order to enroll students. After receiving the report, the Ministry of Education ordered the Peiping Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to supervise the closure and strictly prohibit enrollment. Recently, reports from various parties have indicated that the college's operations have been largely in violation of the Ministry's orders and have cited facts, requesting the Ministry of Education to strictly prohibit it in order to avoid misleading young people.

徐悲鴻對籌備中英藝展意見 217

Xu Beihong's Opinion on the Preparation of the Sino-British Art Exhibition

Xu Beihong expressed his feelings on the Sino-British Art Exhibition, saying, "In Shanghai slang, 'doing something sloppily' is called 'splitting foreign slop.' But this usually refers to individual actions. Even actions by legal persons rarely resemble 'splitting slop.' Only the Sino-British Art Exhibition, which sends national treasures to England without insurance, is truly 'splitting a big slop.' There is no precedent for this. China's attitude of unwavering trust and magnanimity is truly a creative genius, ultimately different from Shanghai tea and silk exporters.

As far as I know, the authorities on Eastern cultural relics in the United Kingdom are Lawrence Binyon, a famous poet, now a major curator at the British Museum, and Yetts, who is skilled in bronzes and is now a professor at the University of London. Neither of them was involved in this matter. Instead, the people sent to China are mostly merchants, which is truly puzzling.

Originally, people asked us to send things to display. Our purpose is to promote culture. I do not agree, because Chinese ancient civilization is universally recognized and does not need promotion. What the British want are things before 1800. If their intention is that China has had no culture since 1800, and even less so in modern times, there is no need for them to choose. Letting them choose is tantamount to declaring that there is no one in our country who knows anything. And the people who came to choose things are not the famous experts there. What is their intention? And we only trust a British diplomatic note and let them handle it. There is no insurance for shipping to England either. What a strange story, what a strange story!

I am one of the special committee members. Naturally, I have never interfered in other people's affairs. But I have witnessed the misfortune of this matter, and the government has solemnly promised it to others. As a modern person, I cannot help but call people's attention. Even something worth thousands of yuan must be insured, and a complete procedure must be negotiated to avoid the possibility of foreign sloppiness. And I hope that the wise government and the great diplomats stationed in England can reach an agreement before the Chinese antiquities are shipped, requiring Britain to come to China next year to hold a British art exhibition, displaying three or four hundred paintings and sculptures. And we declare that we want things after 1800, from Constable and Turner to modern times. It's not that we can't choose, but we let them choose themselves. We humbly ask the British culture for advice, without any hint of 'feeding the milk.'

Brothers Yi Peiji and Li Zongtong are gone. When they were invited to be the director and secretary-general of the Old Palace Museum, it was also believed that they were reliable. It was never expected that they would split such a big slop. It can be said that they were organized from the beginning. Our authorities are mostly gentlemen, but gentlemen can be deceived by their integrity. Those foreign merchants are still able to make ends meet. Don't let Yi Peiji and others sneer. Those innocent and foolish losses of national treasures are completely given away, and they themselves have not enjoyed any of it. Hmph, hmph!"

工部局發表繼續推廣華人教育 220

The Municipal Council Announces Continued Promotion of Chinese Education

▲ 上年度有中小學十所

Ten Primary and Secondary Schools Last Year

▲ 本年內擬再增辦三校

Three More Schools Planned to Be Added This Year

Among the educational affairs of the Public Concession Municipal Council, there are currently 16 council-run schools and 159 private schools that receive subsidies from the Municipal Council. The authorities in charge of education are the Education Committee and the Education Department.

▲ 擬定華人教育方針

Formulating Guidelines for Chinese Education

In 1931, the Education Committee recommended the promotion of Chinese education, planning to open two primary schools each year from that year to 1938, and to establish two girls' secondary schools in 1934. The existing public schools would be completely converted into secondary schools. As for foreign schools, no new schools would be added, only improvements to the existing school buildings and equipment would be made as appropriate. At the same time, subsidies would be granted to private schools with satisfactory operations.

▲ 一九三五擬增三校

Three Schools Planned to Be Added in 1935

However, it is noted that this plan has indeed been adopted in principle by the Board of Directors and the taxpayers' meeting, but it still contains many experimental aspects. It was decided to review the unfinished construction plans at the end of 1934. Due to financial difficulties last year, the matter of adding primary schools was temporarily postponed. At that time, it was suggested that the funds for running schools be used to expand subsidies. The Education Committee then resolved to maintain the current policy, increasing the number of schools as much as financially possible, while continuing to provide subsidies as before, and planned to add two Chinese boys' and girls' primary schools and a second girls' secondary school in 1935.

▲ 女子中學新校完成

New Girls' Secondary School Completed

It is noted that in early 1930, there were only six Chinese schools with only 2,391 students. Currently, there are ten schools with 5,815 students. Since the completion of the Gezhi Public School building in 1928, each secondary school has renovated and expanded its old school buildings to accommodate the increased number of students. Last year, a new three-story school building was built on Singapore Road for a girls' secondary school, which was completed and opened in February this year.

▲ 五處小學最近槪况

Recent Overview of Five Primary Schools

Before 1928, the Municipal Council did not run primary schools, only attaching primary school classes to various public schools. In that year, two primary schools were established. Now there are five schools. One is the Avenue Road Primary School, which was opened in rented houses in 1928 and moved to the old site of the Chinese Public School in 1930. It now has 608 students. One is the Jingzhou Road Primary School, which was also opened in rented houses on Huishan Road in 1928. A new school building was built on Jingzhou Road in 1933, which can accommodate 700 students. The sports field is shared with the Nie Zhongcheng Public School. One is the Xinzha Road Primary School, which was first opened on Edinburgh Road in 1930, and then built its own new school building. The number of students has increased from more than 500 to 725. One is the Ward Road Primary School, which was opened in rented houses after renovation in 1932. The number of students initially was only 242, but has now increased to 731. One is the Huishan Road Primary School, which currently only accepts female students, while male students are sent to Jingzhou Road. This school currently has 400 students.

▲ 創辦簡易補習學校

Establishment of Simple Remedial Schools

Although the Municipal Council has not been able to fully implement the original plan in a short period of time, it has added one girls' secondary school and five primary schools. How the future plans will be implemented depends on the financial situation. In order to remedy the lack of schooling for the children of industry and commerce, a remedial night school was specially established in the Jingzhou Road Primary School in October last year, enrolling more than 260 students, all aged between 14 and 20. The curriculum includes reading, composition, arithmetic, and common sense of citizenship and hygiene. The tuition fee is only five cents per quarter. The students of this school are very enthusiastic about attending, which also shows that such schools are in urgent need.

▲ 學童健康專員檢查

Health Commissioners Inspect School Children

Last year, the council-run schools were in good health. Although some students suffered from infectious diseases, they did not spread in the schools. At the end of 1933, the Health Department drafted a plan to implement physical examinations for students, and immediately started a pilot project in one primary school, finding many cases of eye diseases and skin diseases. The Board of Directors then approved an appropriation of more than 24,000 yuan and appointed a school health commissioner to examine the bodies of school children and provide appropriate treatment for those with diseases, starting with the Chinese primary schools in various districts.

▲ 補助學校一四五所

Subsidizing 145 Schools

Since the Municipal Council decided to subsidize private schools in 1931, the schools receiving subsidies must have satisfactory teaching achievements and comply with the conditions set by the Health Department. As for construction costs, no further assistance will be provided in the future. However, due to health and other needs, modifications to buildings that are required may still be considered. It is estimated that in 1934, there were 145 Chinese private schools subsidized by the Municipal Council, including 24 secondary schools and 121 primary schools, with a total of 31,222 students. The total amount of subsidies was 188,950 yuan.

▲ 外童學校建造新屋

Foreign Children's Schools Build New Houses

According to the report of the Director of Education, the school building of the Western District Western Children's Public School on Route Dufour was completed in January last year and can accommodate 450 students. The McTyeire Girls' School is also expected to be completed by the end of the year and can accommodate 500 students. As for private foreign schools, there are 14 schools subsidized by the Municipal Council, with a total of more than 5,400 students.

The Glory of Guanghua Affiliated High School 221

▲ Awarded Double First Place in Group and Individual Categories in the Current Joint Entrance Examination

The results of the fourth Shanghai Municipal Joint Entrance Examination for Secondary Schools have been officially announced by the Municipal Education Bureau. Guanghua Affiliated High School ranked first among the eighteen high schools in the city participating in the joint entrance examination, meeting the first criterion of the Municipal Education Bureau's reward standards, and will be awarded a prize accordingly. Feng Jifan, a student of the school, ranked first among the more than one hundred and fifty high school students participating in the joint entrance examination, meeting the second criterion of the Municipal Education Bureau's reward standards and will be given a certificate of merit accordingly. In past joint entrance examination results, it was unprecedented for one school to simultaneously win both the group and individual first places. This is because the school's curriculum is rigorous on a daily basis, hence this achievement. It is said that the school will further reorganize from the next semester onwards. The girls will move into new dormitories, and training will be strictly enforced. The gymnasium and science museum are already being prepared for construction. The cooperative will expand its scope, add a credit cooperative, and also plans to construct facilities, all of which are scheduled to be completed before the school's tenth anniversary in June this year.

Publication of "Shanghai School Survey Record" Compiled by Xu Wancheng 223

Mr. Xu Wancheng recently surveyed over two thousand schools in Shanghai, including universities, middle and primary schools, kindergartens, supplementary schools, correspondence schools, and schools established by foreigners. The survey includes detailed information such as school names, addresses, departments or grades, student numbers, library information, and telephone numbers. It took half a year and the assistance of four or five staff members to complete this unprecedented survey in Shanghai. The survey has been compiled into a thick volume called "Shanghai University, Middle and Primary School Survey Record," published by Longwen Bookstore in Dananmen. Mr. Xu is now focusing on surveying universities, middle and primary schools nationwide, including school names, addresses, establishment dates, whether public or private, whether school buildings are self-built or leased, the amount of regular expenses per term, departments and grades, names of current principals and longest-serving faculty members, number of faculty and staff, student numbers, the school's philosophy, library information, and names of librarians. This project has been underway for over a year and is scheduled for publication this autumn. The completion of this book has been greatly supported by over 1,600 education bureau chiefs and education department heads nationwide.

Commercial News 239

Finance 240

Customs Gold Plummets

Selling Sentiment Intensifies in Gold Market

Bulls Once Pushed to 60 Yuan

Ultimately Only a Minor Dip of 8 Jiao

Yesterday's gold market saw a sharp decline in the Central Bank's customs gold unit, which strengthened the selling sentiment. Adding to this, banks had a strong appetite for selling, resulting in a further decline. At one point, the price even broke through the 60 yuan mark. However, with the US Supreme Court about to rule on the gold clause, there was strong demand from buyers of US currency. After a period of easing, the foreign exchange market tightened, making it easier for the gold market to rebound. In the early morning, overseas silver markets were stable in both London and New York. The forward silver market in Montevideo was also stable, with little fluctuation in exchange rates. London spot gold rose by half a penny. In pre-market trading, prices opened steadily at around 63 yuan. Major players took advantage of the high prices to supply. When the Central Bank's official rates were announced, both the British and American rates rose, but the customs gold unit suddenly fell by 1.5 fen. The standard price for bidding gold was reduced to 985.5 yuan, weakening the situation and causing it to decline. The market opened slightly lower in the morning. After the opening, supply and demand balanced, and the market remained stable at first. As banks aggressively sold, prices fell. Anticipating that the HSBC exchange rates for both British and American currencies would be stable, there was some rebound. Later, the banks' appetite for selling continued to be strong, and the foreign exchange market remained loose, leading to increased selling pressure. Major players took advantage of the situation to sell aggressively. At intervals, some bulls emerged, causing the price to gradually fall back into the 60 yuan range. The silver balancing tax was announced unchanged, still levied at 6%. With the British exchange rate calculated at 1 shilling, 5 pence, and 78125, market confidence remained stable, leading to contention around the 60 yuan mark. Subsequently, HSBC and Chase Manhattan took advantage of the low prices to buy, and Chinese merchants regained their buying appetite, causing the foreign exchange market to tighten. Rumors of the Central Bank intervening in the spot market caused a surge of buyers, leading to a rebound. However, there was considerable fluctuation along the way. At this time, the Guangdong group and others made some purchases, seemingly strengthening the market. Later, as banks continued to sell at high prices, the market declined again. Large short sellers also frequently applied pressure, causing the noon close to feel weak. Throughout the morning, the market saw frequent fluctuations, but the overall trend remained mediocre. Cash Circulation Difficult 242

Recently, as the Lunar New Year approaches, most businesses are winding down. Due to the poor economic conditions, circulation and adjustment are quite difficult. As a result, debts are passed on, making it difficult to achieve a satisfactory resolution, leading to a very rigid situation. The financial community is facing this difficult situation and has no way to remedy it. Therefore, there are many who have been affected and suffered losses, and many who have been implicated. Ultimately, many dare not rashly lend, and those in need have no way to raise funds. This can be clearly seen in the interbank lending market. On the surface, foreign interbank lending rates are loose, but that is because there are those who want to lend but no one to borrow from, and those who want to borrow but no one dares to lend to. As a result, there are very few interbank lending transactions. Early morning transactions were only 1.3 to 1.4 million, with new transactions of over 300,000. Afternoon transactions were over 400,000. Transactions among small associations were over 700,000. The foreign interbank lending rate was slightly lower than the previous day, calculated at 8 fen, the same for both morning and afternoon. Adding water to the drawing was also due to the actual surplus of funds, but those who needed funds could not obtain them. Therefore, those with a surplus had more, and those in need remained in need. The foreign mortgage loan transaction took back over 800,000, with new loans of over 900,000. The source of customer funds was 200,000, and the outflow was also 200,000. Over 500,000 in banknotes were recovered, and over 700,000 in circulating notes were issued, along with 400,000 in marked notes. Bank collection and disbursement: Foreign banks collected and disbursed over 2.2 million in bill payments, over 4.89 million in various goods and foreign exchange mortgages and miscellaneous payments, over 1.4 million in foreign exchange settlement payments, over 700,000 in special remittance payments, over 1.4 million in year-end settlement payments, and 600,000 in warehouse withdrawals. Chinese banks collected and disbursed over 3 million in bill payments, over 6.56 million in various goods and foreign exchange mortgages, tax payments, and miscellaneous payments, over 1.8 million in foreign exchange settlement payments, over 800,000 in special remittance payments, over 2.2 million in year-end settlement payments, and 500,000 in warehouse withdrawals. Japanese banks collected and disbursed over 2.78 million in bill payments, over 4.78 million in various goods and foreign exchange miscellaneous payments, over 1.3 million in special remittance payments, over 2.2 million in year-end settlement payments, over 500,000 in foreign exchange settlement payments, and 400,000 in warehouse deposits. Qianzhuang foreign public accounts collected and disbursed over 29 million, foreign withdrawals collected and disbursed over 3.8 million, various remittance payments over 400,000, and over 700,000 in cash collections. Also, the total number of exchanges at the city's clearing house on the 23rd was 10,048,652.04 yuan, including 5,300,080.83 yuan in silver dollars and 5,185,724.21 yuan in foreign exchange transfers.

Grains

Many Short Positions Eager to Unload This Month's Flour 254

Distant Months Also Seeing Strong Selling Pressure

Yesterday, the flour market uniformly declined after opening in the morning. Quotations for foreign wheat showed a decline of 2.0 jiao in Chicago and around 2.4 jiao in Canada. At the opening, short positions for the current month, due to the nearing of delivery, were eagerly liquidated. Moreover, as factories still held a significant amount of hedging positions and were unwilling to unwind them, market sentiment weakened. Distant months also declined due to the unfavorable foreign wheat situation and a large number of short positions. The market atmosphere loosened. By the afternoon opening, the situation for the current month deteriorated further. Hedgers had to deliver goods, and with the tight credit conditions, there were fewer new hedgers to take their place, leading to lower prices. Distant months also continued to fall step by step due to strong selling pressure. According to market insiders, if hedgers do not cover their positions for the current month and short positions need to be closed urgently, there may still be problems. As a result, the current month fell by 3.75 fen, February fell by 3.5 fen, March fell by 3 fen, April and May fell by 2.75 fen, and June fell by 1.75 fen.

Distant Month Wheat Slightly Sold Short 255

Yesterday, the futures wheat market was generally quiet in all months after opening in the morning. Although foreign wheat quotations continued to decline slightly by about 2.4 jiao, there was little movement due to only two trading days left before the settlement date, and outside speculators had already stopped participating. Market insiders had also closed their positions. By the afternoon opening, trading became even more scarce. The February contract was offered at a loss in every transaction, while the March and April contracts saw more short selling, making the market atmosphere unstable. However, the volume was very small, and fluctuations were minimal. As a result, February fell by 4 fen, March fell by 4 fen, and April fell by 1 fen. Spot wheat lacked interest from factories, and traders also feared that settlements would have to wait until the market reopened after the Spring Festival.

▲ There are rumors that the Canadian government plans to provide a subsidy of 1.5 jiao for wheat exports, which is unfavorable to markets worldwide and could break through U.S. tariff barriers and enter the market.

Rice Market in Southern Shanghai Shows Good Performance 256

(Southern Shanghai) Yesterday, supplies from various regions increased, totaling over 50 shipments (over 9,000 shi of goods). Sales in the local market were brisk, and bulk purchases continued, such as the Qingdao traders buying 600-700 bags. Therefore, the market improved, and the situation tightened. Thick japonica and late rice varieties saw gains of several jiao. However, with the approaching major settlement period, significant changes seem unlikely. Du Jian rice has been in short supply for several days and is now particularly popular. Foreign Jian rice remains inactive. Yin Bian Yuan rice is still stable.

(Northern Shanghai) Yesterday, over 20 shipments arrived from various regions in the He Xia area. Sales of various types of rice in the market showed slight improvement. White japonica saw some trading, while thin rice sold slightly better. Remaining goods were slow. Market prices saw a slight increase for white japonica, while Bian Yuan and various Jian varieties declined by several fen. Thin rice saw little fluctuation.

Low-Priced Ke Xian Rice Sold; Foreign Rice Situation Settled 257

Yesterday, the foreign rice market saw sluggish sales of Ke rice. In the general market, only 500 bags of Saigon broken rice were traded. As traders in various regions are closing their books for the year, purchasing interest is gradually fading. However, there were still inquiries in the local market, with a transaction of over 1,000 bags of Saigon first-grade rice and a trade of 800 tons of futures broken rice. The market is temporarily stable. As production prices have been firm for a long time, cargo owners are very confident and are unwilling to sell at low prices despite having a large inventory. The market may stabilize within the year. However, with traders eager to close their books, sales of Ke Xian rice have been slow. Only 700-800 bags were offered on the previous day. Yesterday, cargo owners lowered prices to encourage sales, which resulted in 2,600 bags being offered, but prices were 5 fen to 1 jiao lower than the previous market. The He Xia rice market is scheduled to close on the 28th, so the local market for foreign Ke Xian rice may be lively for now.

Miscellaneous Grain Market Already Closing 258

Yesterday, trading in the miscellaneous grain market was scarce. The overall situation was that partial closures were already taking place. The soybean market initially weakened due to sluggish sales. In the afternoon, news of sharp gains in distant-month contracts slightly improved sentiment, but trading remained sparse. Overall, factories purchased 600 bags of Guide soybeans at a price of 3 yuan 9 jiao, and two carloads of Dalian Siping Street soybeans at a price of 4 yuan 2 jiao 5 fen. In addition, one carload of large-grain soybeans was offered at 4 yuan 3 jiao. The local market traded 700 bags of Hankou Zha soybeans at a price of 3 yuan 7 jiao 7 fen and 6 jiao 7 fen, and over 300 bags of Dalian Fanjiatun soybeans at a price of 4 yuan 4 jiao.

Sugar Market

Guangdong Coarse White Sugar Further Reduced by 2 Jiao 259

Yesterday, the sugar market showed a more sluggish trend, with very few transactions. The guild's quotations for Grade 24 coarse white sugar and Dutch red sugar received no bids. The previously arrived Guangdong coarse white sugar continued to be auctioned yesterday. The original amount was 2,460 bags, and the price was reduced by another 2 jiao to 18 yuan 3 jiao. Only 70 bags were transacted, indicating the weakness of the market. Chaoqing sugar continued to be offered at 21-2,300 bags, with little fluctuation. Huanggang Qing sugar was priced at 10 yuan 1 jiao 2 fen, and Longqing Jiang sugar was priced at 9 yuan 8 jiao.

North-South Goods

Hunan Lotus Seeds Price Rebound 260

Hunan lotus seeds have not had a chance to rebound recently due to the lack of large-scale sales in the Shanghai market. However, according to a letter from Hankou, inventories in the production area have become thin. Despite the approaching major settlement period, sales have been active, leading to a price increase of 7-8 jiao. At the same time, prices in the production area have also increased by 6 jiao. Market sentiment here has also tightened slightly. It is expected that the first trading day after the settlement period will see a recovery.

Metals

Enamel Factories Pre-Purchase Futures Black Iron Sheets 261

The black iron sheet market has been very weak recently. Although holders are making every effort to attract buyers, the unfavorable environment has made sales difficult. However, well-capitalized enamel factories, seeing that current prices for these goods are low, have been actively paying deposits to order futures for delivery in the coming spring. 500 bundles of 2-foot 6-inch 18-gauge prime grade sheets were transacted at a price of 9 yuan 5 jiao, and 1,000 bundles of secondary grade sheets were transacted at a price of 8 yuan 5 jiao. 250 bundles of 3-foot 6-gauge to 13-gauge sheets were transacted at a price of 9 yuan 6 jiao. It is said that these transactions were sold by metal shops in the North Suzhou Road area.
